أما صنة التكوين فإن الماتريدي وأصحابه يعتبرونها صفة حقيقية قديمة قائمة بذات الله زائدة على ذاته بينما هي عند الأشاعرة صفة إضافية حادثة ومتجددة بتجدد الأفعال شأنها في ذلك شأن كل صفات الفعل التي هي عند الأشاعرة حادثة بحدوث الأفعال . وقد أثبت الماتريدية صفة التكوين وقالوا بأنها الصفة التي تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات وتدثر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، وقصر وا تعلق صفة القدرة بصحة وجود المخلوق، لأن القدرة تتعلق بالممكنات حال كونها ممكنات ولكن لا شأن لها بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تؤثر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود لأن ذلك وظيفة صفة التكوين أو التخليق . يقول النسفي في التبصرة : " ولا يقال إنه اختص بالوجود بعد العدم بمعنى هو غيره وهو قدرة الباري جل جلاله ؛ لأن القدرة تقتضي كون ما يدخل تحتها مقدوراً ، لا تقتضي كونه موجوداً : ولو اقتضى كونه موجوداً لكان إيجاداً ؛ إذ الإيجاد يوجب الوجود ، وليس المقدور بموجود لا محالة ، ولهذا يوصف المعدوم بأنه مقدور ، ولأن الوجود لو حصل بالقدرة لم يكن بنا حاجة إلى القول بالخلق والإيجاد ، فكان الله تعالى قادرا على العالم، لا خالقا له ولا موجد ا ٢٠ . وبقول في موضع آخر والوقوع متى يكون بالنادرة ، الوقوع بالإيقاع والوجود بالإنجاد ، والقددة ليكون الفاعل في فعلة مختارا غير مضطر ،٣ . ومن البين أن علة هذا الاختيار أو علة كون الله قادراً هو الإمكان العائد إلى الممكن بحسب ماهيته ، إذ الممكن هو ولذلك تعلقت به القدرة، لأن الأشياء لو كانت واجبة عامه ، وجوده وما يصيح أو ممتنعة لانتفت القدرة عليها . ما يصيح أما الأشعرية فيرون أن القدرة هي الصفة المتعلقة بإيجاد الأشياء والمؤثرة في
As for the attribute of takwin (causation), the Maturidi and his followers consider it a real eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, superadded to His essence, while according to the Ash'aris it is a contingent attribute, originated and renewed with the renewal of acts, like all attributes of action which according to the Ash'aris are originated with the origination of acts. And the Maturidis affirmed the attribute of takwin and said that it is the attribute that pertains to bringing possible things into existence and [؟] in bringing them out from non-existence to existence, and they restricted the relation of the attribute of power (qudra) to the soundness of the existence of the creature, because power relates to possible things as they are possible but it has no concern with bringing possible things into existence and does not affect their bringing out from non-existence to existence, because that is the function of the attribute of takwin or creation (takhlīq). Al-Nasafi says in al-Tabṣira: "And it is not said that it (existence) is specifically after non-existence in the sense that it is other than Him, and it is the power of the Blessed and Exalted; because power requires that what falls under it be possible (maqdur), it does not require that it be existent: if it required it to be existent, it would be bringing into existence (ījād); because bringing into existence necessitates existence, and the possible is not necessarily existent, and for this reason the non-existent is described as possible (maqdur). And because if existence were obtained by power, we would have no need to speak of creation (khalq) and bringing into existence (ījād), so God Almighty would be powerful over the world, not its creator nor its bringer into existence." And he says in another place: "And occurrence (wuqūʿ) is at times by chance; occurrence is by making occur (īqāʿ) and existence is by bringing into existence (īnjād); and power [؟] so that the agent in His act is choice not compelled." And it is clear that the cause of this choice or the cause of God being powerful is contingency (imkān) belonging to the possible according to its quiddity, for the possible is [؟] and therefore power relates to it, because if things were necessary or impossible, power would be negated over them. [؟] As for the Ash'aris, they hold that power is the attribute related to bringing things into existence and is effective in
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a detailed doctrinal comparison on the attribute of takwin (causation/creating). It begins by stating the Maturidi position: takwin is a real (haqiqiyya), eternal (qadima) attribute superadded to God's essence, while the Ash'aris consider it a contingent (idafiyya) attribute that is originated and renewed with each act, like all attributes of action. The Maturidis affirm takwin as the specific attribute responsible for bringing possible beings from non-existence into existence, and they restrict the role of qudra (power) to mere possibility (sihhat al-wujud or being 'maqdur'). They argue that power does not necessitate existence, but only possibility. The passage then quotes al-Nasafi's Tabṣira to provide a logical proof: if power directly caused existence, then there would be no need to speak of creation or bringing into existence; God would only be 'powerful' over the world, not its 'creator.' This proves the need for a separate attribute of takwin. The passage then quotes al-Nasafi again on the relationship between occurrence and power, emphasizing that God's power relates to possibles based on their contingency (imkan). Finally, it contrasts with the Ash'ari view that power itself is the attribute that brings things into existence. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidis deny qudra's role in creation entirely.
Correction: The Maturidis hold that qudra relates to possibility, not actual existence; takwin is the attribute that brings things into existence.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view presented in the passage, what is the function of the attribute of qudra (power)?
A) To bring possible things into existence.
B) To relate to possible things as possible, not to necessitate their existence.
C) To create ex nihilo.
D) To be identical with takwin.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis distinguish between qudra (power), which relates to possibility, and takwin (causation), which brings existents into being, to maintain God's sovereignty and the contingency of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life have you implicitly reduced God to 'powerful' but not 'creator'—trusting in your own ability or secondary causes rather than actively relying on His direct act of bringing things into being? What would change if you consciously invoked His attribute of takwin in that situation today?
?
The Maturidis insist that God is both powerful (qādir) and creator (khāliq). Is there a part of your soul that knows God can do something, yet doubts His active creation of that outcome for you right now? What is one concrete fear or hope you need to entrust to His takwin instead of your own planning?
?
If the attribute of takwin is what truly brings everything from non-existence into existence, then every breath you take is a direct act of God's creation. How does that reality confront your sense of self-sufficiency? What practical step can you take today to live with the awareness that God alone sustains your existence moment by moment?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
The Dispute over Takwin: Is Bringing into Existence a Distinct Attribute?
Maturidi and Ash'ari views on takwin and qudra, with al-Nasafi's argument and the conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi and Ash'ari positions on the attribute of takwin and how they relate to power (qudra).

Core Idea
Takwin is the attribute that brings possibles into existence; power only makes them possible.

This lesson explores a key difference between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools regarding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Maturidis argue that takwin is a distinct eternal attribute, while the Ash'aris see it as a mode of power. Understanding this dispute sheds light on the broader divergence over attributes of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on takwin
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the Maturidi argument and the quote from al-Nasafi.
2
Identify the two views
Contrast the Maturidi view that takwin is distinct from qudra with the Ash'ari view that qudra suffices.
3
Analyze al-Nasafi's argument
Understand why al-Nasafi argues that power cannot bring into existence; otherwise God would not be creator.
4
Understand the Ash'ari two-attachment theory
Learn the distinction between suitability-attachment (suluhi) and actualizing-attachment (tanjizi).
5
Reflect on the secondary nature of the dispute
Note that both schools agree on the principle of superadded attributes.

مقدمة الماتريدية الذين ينكرون أن يكون البقاء صفة زائدة على ذات الباقي ، كما ينكره بعض الأشاعرة كإمام الحرمين وفخر الدين الرازي . أما صفة التكوين فإن الماتريدي وأصحابه يعتبرونها صفة حقيقية قديمة قائمة بذات الله زائدة على ذاته بينما هي عند الأشاعرة صفة إضافية حادثة ومتجددة بتجدد الأفعال شأنها في ذلك شأن كل صفات الفعل التي هي عند الأشاعرة حادثة بحدوث الأفعال . وقد أثبت الماتريدية صفة التكوين وقالوا بأنها الصفة التي تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات وتظهر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، وقصروا تعلق صفة القدرة بصحة وجود المخلوق، لأن القدرة تتعلق بالممكنات حال كونها ممكنات ولكن لا شأن لها بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تؤثر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود لأن ذلك وظيفة صفة التكوين أو التخليق . يقول النسفي في التبصرة : " ولا يقال إنه اختص بالوجود بعد العدم بمعنى هو غيره وهو قدرة الباري جل جلاله ؛ لأن القدرة تقتضي كون ما يدخل تحتها مقدوراً ، لا تقتضي كونه موجوداً : ولو اقتضى كونه موجوداً لكان إيجاداً ؛ إذ الإيجاد يوجب الوجود ، وليس المقدور بموجود لا محالة ، ولهذا يوصف المعدوم بأنه مقدور ، ولأن الوجود لو حصل بالقدرة لم يكن بنا حاجة إلى القول بالخلق والإيجاد ، فكان الله تعالى قادرا على العالم، لا خالقا له ولا موجدا . ويقول في موضع آخر الوقوع متى يكون بالقدرة ، الوقوع بالإيقاع والوجود بالإيجاد ، والقدرة تكون الفاعل في فعله مختارا غير مضطر . ومن البين أن علة هذا الاختيار أو علة كون الله قادراً هو الإمكان العائد إلى الممكن بحسب ماهيته ، إذ الممكن هو ولذلك تعلقت به القدرة ، لأن الأشياء لو كانت واجبة أو ممتنعة لانتفت القدرة عليها .

أما الأشعرية فيرون أن القدرة هي الصفة المتعلقة بإيجاد الأشياء والمؤثرة في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، غاية ما هناك أن هذا التعلق متوقف على انضمام الإرادة وتابع للعلم، بمعنى أن ما علم الله وجوده يوجد منه بقدرته ، والإرادة تخصص زمان الوقوع . وليس التكوين إلا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور عند إرادة الله إيجاده ، ثمة كانت صفة نسبية حادثة . فالقدرة عند الأشاعرة لها تعلقان : تعلق صلوحي قديم ، وهو تعلقها بصحة وجود الأشياء ، والآخر تعلق تنجيزي حادث ، وليس التكوين هذا التعلق التنجيزي الحادث الذي هو نفس إخراج الأشياء من العدم إلى الوجود . وعلى ذلك لا يرى الأشعرية معنى لإثبات التكوين صفة زائدة لا فائدة فيها ، لأن القدرة هي الصفة المؤثرة في إيجاد الأشياء . فوراء الاختلاف في صفة التكوين اختلاف في صفات الفعل ، واختلاف في صفة القدرة ووظيفتها . لكن هذه كلها خلافات في التفاريع ، ولا يخرج واحد من دائرة أهل السنة لأنه اختلف أصحابه في تفاريع المذهب ، لأن الأصل ثابت ومتفق عليه وهو إجماع أهل السنة على إثبات الصفات الزائدة على الذات كمعاني قديمة لا هي الذات ولا هي غير الذات .

ويتفق أهل السنة على أن كلام الله تعالى صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته مفرقين بين كلامه النفسي الذي هو صفة له قديمة وبين الحروف والأصوات الدالة على كلامه النفسي وهي عندهم حادثة . ثم يختلفون بعد ذلك حول جواز سماع كلامه النفسي . فالأشعري ومعظم أصحابه يقولون بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، واعتمد على ذلك سند من العقل والنقل. أما العقل فقد استند الأشعري في دعواه على جواز سماع كلام الله على نفس الأساس الذي استند عليه في جواز رؤية الله . فكما أن علة جواز كونه مرئياً هي وجوده ، فكذلك وجود الكلام النفسي هو علة جواز سماعه . أما النقل فيتمسك الأشعري بقوله تعالى : " وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ " (التوبة: 6) .
Introduction: The Maturidis who deny that baqa' (permanence) is an attribute superadded to the essence of the Eternal, just as some Ash'aris deny it, such as Imam al-Haramayn and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. As for the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence), al-Maturidi and his companions consider it a real, eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, superadded to His essence, while according to the Ash'aris it is a relational, originated attribute, renewed with the renewal of actions, like all attributes of action which according to the Ash'aris are originated with the origination of actions. The Maturidis affirmed the attribute of takwin and said that it is the attribute that pertains to bringing possibles into existence and bringing them forth from non-existence to existence, and they limited the attachment of the attribute of qudra (power) to the soundness of the existence of the creature, because qudra attaches to possibles as possibles, but it has no role in bringing possibles into existence, nor does it attach to bringing them into existence, nor does it effect their bringing forth from non-existence to existence, because that is the function of the attribute of takwin or khalq (creation). Al-Nasafi says in al-Tabsira: "And it is not said that it (the thing) is specially distinguished by existence after non-existence in the sense that it is other than Him and it is the power of the Almighty; because power requires that what enters under it be possible (maqdur), it does not require that it be existent: if it required that it be existent, it would be bringing into existence (ijad); since bringing into existence necessitates existence, and the possible is not necessarily existent, and therefore non-existent is described as possible, and because if existence were obtained by power, we would have no need to speak of creation and bringing into existence, so God would be powerful over the world, not its creator nor its bringer into existence." And he says in another place: "Occurrence is only by power; occurrence is by making occur and existence is by bringing into existence; and power makes the agent in his act free and not compelled. And it is evident that the cause of this choice or the cause of God's being powerful is the contingency (imkan) returning to the possible according to its quiddity; for the possible is that, and therefore power attaches to it; because if things were necessary or impossible, power over them would be negated."

As for the Ash'aris, they hold that qudra is the attribute pertaining to bringing things into existence and effecting their bringing forth from non-existence to existence, except that this attachment is dependent on the joining of will and subordinate to knowledge, meaning that what God knows to exist, He brings into existence by His power, and the will specifies the time of occurrence. And takwin is nothing but the attachment of power to the possible when God wills to bring it into existence; thus it is a relative, originated attribute. For power according to the Ash'aris has two attachments: an eternal suitability-attachment (ta'alluq suluhi qadim), which is its attachment to the soundness of existence of things, and another originated actualizing-attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith), and takwin is this originated actualizing-attachment which is precisely the bringing out of things from non-existence to existence. Therefore the Ash'aris see no meaning in affirming takwin as a superadded attribute with no benefit, because qudra is the attribute that effects the bringing into existence of things. So behind the difference over the attribute of takwin is a difference over the attributes of action, and a difference over the attribute of qudra and its function. But all these are differences in secondary branches (tafari'), and none of them depart from the circle of Ahl al-Sunna, because its adherents differ in the secondary branches of the school, since the principle is established and agreed upon, namely the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna on affirming attributes superadded to the essence as eternal meanings, neither identical to the essence nor other than it.

And Ahl al-Sunna agree that the speech of God is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between His internal speech (kalam nafsi) which is an eternal attribute of His, and the letters and sounds that indicate His internal speech, which according to them are originated. Then they differ after that concerning the permissibility of hearing His internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers hold the permissibility of hearing internal speech, and they relied on a proof from intellect and transmitted evidence. As for the intellect, al-Ash'ari based his claim on the permissibility of hearing God's speech on the same basis on which he based the permissibility of seeing God. For just as the cause of the permissibility of His being seen is His existence, so the existence of internal speech is the cause of the permissibility of hearing it. As for transmitted evidence, al-Ash'ari adheres to His saying: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Al-Tawba 9:6).
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage provides a comparative exposition of differences between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools on several divine attributes, while affirming that both remain within the fold of Ahl al-Sunna. It begins by noting that the Maturidis, like some Ash'aris (e.g., Imam al-Haramayn and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi), deny that baqa' (permanence) is an attribute superadded to the essence of the Eternal. Then it turns to the central dispute over the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Maturidis consider takwin a real, eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, superadded to it, while the Ash'aris view it as a relational, originated attribute renewed with actions, like all attributes of action. The Maturidis argue that takwin is the specific attribute that brings possibles from non-existence to existence; qudra (power) only attaches to the soundness of existence or to the possible as possible, but does not effect existence. To support this, the author cites al-Nasafi's al-Tabsira, where al-Nasafi argues that if power necessitated existence, then everything possible would always exist, which is false; rather, power only makes things possible, not existent. Without a distinct attribute of bringing into existence, God would be 'powerful over the world, but not its creator'. Al-Nasafi also notes that contingency (imkan) is the basis for power, as necessity or impossibility would negate power.

The Ash'ari counter-view is then presented: qudra is the attribute that brings things into existence, but it is dependent on will and knowledge; the will specifies the time. For Ash'aris, power has two attachments: an eternal suitability-attachment (ta'alluq suluhi) concerning the possibility of the thing, and an originated actualizing-attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi) that is precisely takwin. Thus takwin is not a distinct attribute but a mode of power's attachment. They see no benefit in affirming an extra attribute. The passage concludes that these are all differences in secondary branches (tafari'), not fundamental, because all Ahl al-Sunna agree on affirming superadded attributes that are neither identical to the essence nor other than it.

The second part deals with God's speech (kalam). All Ahl al-Sunna agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the originated letters/sounds that express it. The dispute is over the permissibility of hearing God's internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most Ash'aris permit it, using both rational and transmitted proof. Their rational proof is analogous to the proof for seeing God: just as God's existence makes vision possible, His internal speech's existence makes hearing it possible. The transmitted proof is the verse in which the polytheist is granted protection 'so that he may hear the word of Allah,' interpreted as referring to the internal speech heard by Moses or others as a miracle.

Key Terms
تكوين (takwin)
قدرة (qudra)
تعلق صلوحي (suitability-attachment)
تعلق تنجيزي (actualizing-attachment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi-Ash'ari difference on takwin is a fundamental split in Ahl al-Sunna.
Correction: The text states that these are differences in secondary branches (tafari'), and all agree on the principle of superadded eternal attributes.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi as cited in the passage, what would be the consequence if qudra (power) necessitated existence?
A) God would be both powerful and creator, but not eternal.
B) There would be no need to affirm a distinct attribute of takwin (bringing into existence).
C) God would be powerful over the world but not its creator nor its bringer into existence.
D) God would be compelled to create, removing free will.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over takwin is a secondary difference within Ahl al-Sunna, rooted in whether bringing into existence is a distinct attribute or a mode of power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that al-Nasafi argued that if power alone brought things into existence, we would have no need to speak of creation. In your daily life, do you truly experience God's act of bringing you into existence moment by moment, or do you take your own existence for granted? What would change if you woke each morning conscious that you are being created anew?
?
The Ash'aris say that God's power creates when joined with will and knowledge. Do you live as if every event in your life is directly willed and created by God, or do you attribute things to secondary causes? Examine your worry about the future: does it stem from forgetting that God's power is actively creating every outcome?
?
This lesson concludes that the difference over takwin is a secondary issue within Ahl al-Sunna. Are there theological disagreements where you tend to treat brothers and sisters as outsiders? Can you identify a specific difference you have with another Muslim that, in light of this passage, might be a 'tafri' (branch) rather than a root? Will you commit to changing your attitude toward them?

The Eternal Speech of God: Kalam Nafsi and the Possibility of Hearing It
Agreement on kalam nafsi and the Ash'ari proof for hearing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the agreement of Ahl al-Sunna on God's speech as an eternal attribute, and the Ash'ari argument for the permissibility of hearing it.

Core Idea
God's eternal internal speech can be heard, just as His essence can be seen.

This lesson examines the second major topic in the passage: the nature of God's speech. All Ahl al-Sunna affirm that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the created letters and sounds. The point of disagreement is whether this internal speech can be heard. Al-Ash'ari argues yes, using rational and scriptural proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on kalam
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the agreement on kalam nafsi and the difference on hearing it.
2
Identify the two types of speech
Distinguish between kalam nafsi (eternal) and the letters/sounds (originated).
3
Understand the rational proof
Al-Ash'ari analogizes hearing kalam nafsi to seeing God: existence makes it possible.
4
Understand the scriptural proof
The verse from Surah al-Tawba is interpreted as referring to hearing internal speech.

مقدمة الماتريدية الذين ينكرون أن يكون البقاء صفة زائدة على ذات الباقي ، كما ينكره بعض الأشاعرة كإمام الحرمين وفخر الدين الرازي . أما صفة التكوين فإن الماتريدي وأصحابه يعتبرونها صفة حقيقية قديمة قائمة بذات الله زائدة على ذاته بينما هي عند الأشاعرة صفة إضافية حادثة ومتجددة بتجدد الأفعال شأنها في ذلك شأن كل صفات الفعل التي هي عند الأشاعرة حادثة بحدوث الأفعال . وقد أثبت الماتريدية صفة التكوين وقالوا بأنها الصفة التي تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات وتظهر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، وقصروا تعلق صفة القدرة بصحة وجود المخلوق، لأن القدرة تتعلق بالممكنات حال كونها ممكنات ولكن لا شأن لها بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تتعلق بإيجاد الممكنات ولا تؤثر في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود لأن ذلك وظيفة صفة التكوين أو التخليق . يقول النسفي في التبصرة : " ولا يقال إنه اختص بالوجود بعد العدم بمعنى هو غيره وهو قدرة الباري جل جلاله ؛ لأن القدرة تقتضي كون ما يدخل تحتها مقدوراً ، لا تقتضي كونه موجوداً : ولو اقتضى كونه موجوداً لكان إيجاداً ؛ إذ الإيجاد يوجب الوجود ، وليس المقدور بموجود لا محالة ، ولهذا يوصف المعدوم بأنه مقدور ، ولأن الوجود لو حصل بالقدرة لم يكن بنا حاجة إلى القول بالخلق والإيجاد ، فكان الله تعالى قادرا على العالم، لا خالقا له ولا موجدا . ويقول في موضع آخر الوقوع متى يكون بالقدرة ، الوقوع بالإيقاع والوجود بالإيجاد ، والقدرة تكون الفاعل في فعله مختارا غير مضطر . ومن البين أن علة هذا الاختيار أو علة كون الله قادراً هو الإمكان العائد إلى الممكن بحسب ماهيته ، إذ الممكن هو ولذلك تعلقت به القدرة ، لأن الأشياء لو كانت واجبة أو ممتنعة لانتفت القدرة عليها .

أما الأشعرية فيرون أن القدرة هي الصفة المتعلقة بإيجاد الأشياء والمؤثرة في إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، غاية ما هناك أن هذا التعلق متوقف على انضمام الإرادة وتابع للعلم، بمعنى أن ما علم الله وجوده يوجد منه بقدرته ، والإرادة تخصص زمان الوقوع . وليس التكوين إلا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور عند إرادة الله إيجاده ، ثمة كانت صفة نسبية حادثة . فالقدرة عند الأشاعرة لها تعلقان : تعلق صلوحي قديم ، وهو تعلقها بصحة وجود الأشياء ، والآخر تعلق تنجيزي حادث ، وليس التكوين هذا التعلق التنجيزي الحادث الذي هو نفس إخراج الأشياء من العدم إلى الوجود . وعلى ذلك لا يرى الأشعرية معنى لإثبات التكوين صفة زائدة لا فائدة فيها ، لأن القدرة هي الصفة المؤثرة في إيجاد الأشياء . فوراء الاختلاف في صفة التكوين اختلاف في صفات الفعل ، واختلاف في صفة القدرة ووظيفتها . لكن هذه كلها خلافات في التفاريع ، ولا يخرج واحد من دائرة أهل السنة لأنه اختلف أصحابه في تفاريع المذهب ، لأن الأصل ثابت ومتفق عليه وهو إجماع أهل السنة على إثبات الصفات الزائدة على الذات كمعاني قديمة لا هي الذات ولا هي غير الذات .

ويتفق أهل السنة على أن كلام الله تعالى صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته مفرقين بين كلامه النفسي الذي هو صفة له قديمة وبين الحروف والأصوات الدالة على كلامه النفسي وهي عندهم حادثة . ثم يختلفون بعد ذلك حول جواز سماع كلامه النفسي . فالأشعري ومعظم أصحابه يقولون بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، واعتمد على ذلك سند من العقل والنقل. أما العقل فقد استند الأشعري في دعواه على جواز سماع كلام الله على نفس الأساس الذي استند عليه في جواز رؤية الله . فكما أن علة جواز كونه مرئياً هي وجوده ، فكذلك وجود الكلام النفسي هو علة جواز سماعه . أما النقل فيتمسك الأشعري بقوله تعالى : " وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ " (التوبة: 6) .
Introduction: The Maturidis who deny that baqa' (permanence) is an attribute superadded to the essence of the Eternal, just as some Ash'aris deny it, such as Imam al-Haramayn and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. As for the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence), al-Maturidi and his companions consider it a real, eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, superadded to His essence, while according to the Ash'aris it is a relational, originated attribute, renewed with the renewal of actions, like all attributes of action which according to the Ash'aris are originated with the origination of actions. The Maturidis affirmed the attribute of takwin and said that it is the attribute that pertains to bringing possibles into existence and bringing them forth from non-existence to existence, and they limited the attachment of the attribute of qudra (power) to the soundness of the existence of the creature, because qudra attaches to possibles as possibles, but it has no role in bringing possibles into existence, nor does it attach to bringing them into existence, nor does it effect their bringing forth from non-existence to existence, because that is the function of the attribute of takwin or khalq (creation). Al-Nasafi says in al-Tabsira: "And it is not said that it (the thing) is specially distinguished by existence after non-existence in the sense that it is other than Him and it is the power of the Almighty; because power requires that what enters under it be possible (maqdur), it does not require that it be existent: if it required that it be existent, it would be bringing into existence (ijad); since bringing into existence necessitates existence, and the possible is not necessarily existent, and therefore non-existent is described as possible, and because if existence were obtained by power, we would have no need to speak of creation and bringing into existence, so God would be powerful over the world, not its creator nor its bringer into existence." And he says in another place: "Occurrence is only by power; occurrence is by making occur and existence is by bringing into existence; and power makes the agent in his act free and not compelled. And it is evident that the cause of this choice or the cause of God's being powerful is the contingency (imkan) returning to the possible according to its quiddity; for the possible is that, and therefore power attaches to it; because if things were necessary or impossible, power over them would be negated."

As for the Ash'aris, they hold that qudra is the attribute pertaining to bringing things into existence and effecting their bringing forth from non-existence to existence, except that this attachment is dependent on the joining of will and subordinate to knowledge, meaning that what God knows to exist, He brings into existence by His power, and the will specifies the time of occurrence. And takwin is nothing but the attachment of power to the possible when God wills to bring it into existence; thus it is a relative, originated attribute. For power according to the Ash'aris has two attachments: an eternal suitability-attachment (ta'alluq suluhi qadim), which is its attachment to the soundness of existence of things, and another originated actualizing-attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith), and takwin is this originated actualizing-attachment which is precisely the bringing out of things from non-existence to existence. Therefore the Ash'aris see no meaning in affirming takwin as a superadded attribute with no benefit, because qudra is the attribute that effects the bringing into existence of things. So behind the difference over the attribute of takwin is a difference over the attributes of action, and a difference over the attribute of qudra and its function. But all these are differences in secondary branches (tafari'), and none of them depart from the circle of Ahl al-Sunna, because its adherents differ in the secondary branches of the school, since the principle is established and agreed upon, namely the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna on affirming attributes superadded to the essence as eternal meanings, neither identical to the essence nor other than it.

And Ahl al-Sunna agree that the speech of God is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between His internal speech (kalam nafsi) which is an eternal attribute of His, and the letters and sounds that indicate His internal speech, which according to them are originated. Then they differ after that concerning the permissibility of hearing His internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers hold the permissibility of hearing internal speech, and they relied on a proof from intellect and transmitted evidence. As for the intellect, al-Ash'ari based his claim on the permissibility of hearing God's speech on the same basis on which he based the permissibility of seeing God. For just as the cause of the permissibility of His being seen is His existence, so the existence of internal speech is the cause of the permissibility of hearing it. As for transmitted evidence, al-Ash'ari adheres to His saying: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Al-Tawba 9:6).
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage provides a comparative exposition of differences between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools on several divine attributes, while affirming that both remain within the fold of Ahl al-Sunna. It begins by noting that the Maturidis, like some Ash'aris (e.g., Imam al-Haramayn and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi), deny that baqa' (permanence) is an attribute superadded to the essence of the Eternal. Then it turns to the central dispute over the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Maturidis consider takwin a real, eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, superadded to it, while the Ash'aris view it as a relational, originated attribute renewed with actions, like all attributes of action. The Maturidis argue that takwin is the specific attribute that brings possibles from non-existence to existence; qudra (power) only attaches to the soundness of existence or to the possible as possible, but does not effect existence. To support this, the author cites al-Nasafi's al-Tabsira, where al-Nasafi argues that if power necessitated existence, then everything possible would always exist, which is false; rather, power only makes things possible, not existent. Without a distinct attribute of bringing into existence, God would be 'powerful over the world, but not its creator'. Al-Nasafi also notes that contingency (imkan) is the basis for power, as necessity or impossibility would negate power.

The Ash'ari counter-view is then presented: qudra is the attribute that brings things into existence, but it is dependent on will and knowledge; the will specifies the time. For Ash'aris, power has two attachments: an eternal suitability-attachment (ta'alluq suluhi) concerning the possibility of the thing, and an originated actualizing-attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi) that is precisely takwin. Thus takwin is not a distinct attribute but a mode of power's attachment. They see no benefit in affirming an extra attribute. The passage concludes that these are all differences in secondary branches (tafari'), not fundamental, because all Ahl al-Sunna agree on affirming superadded attributes that are neither identical to the essence nor other than it.

The second part deals with God's speech (kalam). All Ahl al-Sunna agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the originated letters/sounds that express it. The dispute is over the permissibility of hearing God's internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most Ash'aris permit it, using both rational and transmitted proof. Their rational proof is analogous to the proof for seeing God: just as God's existence makes vision possible, His internal speech's existence makes hearing it possible. The transmitted proof is the verse in which the polytheist is granted protection 'so that he may hear the word of Allah,' interpreted as referring to the internal speech heard by Moses or others as a miracle.

Key Terms
كلام نفسي (kalam nafsi)
حروف (letters)
أصوات (sounds)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari view on hearing God's speech is universally rejected by all Sunnis.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari and most Ash'aris hold it permissible, and they provide rational and scriptural proofs.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari's rational proof for hearing God's internal speech, what is the cause of its permissibility?
A) Its contingency
B) Its existence
C) Its divine origin
D) Its eternity

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school permits hearing God's eternal internal speech, basing this on the same principle as the vision of God: existence makes perception possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's speech is eternal and not created? How does that affect how you approach the Quran each day?
?
If hearing God's eternal speech is possible simply because it exists, what does that imply for your desire to hear His speech in this life or the next? Are you genuinely longing for that, or content with created words?
?
The polytheist was granted protection 'so that he may hear the word of Allah.' How seriously do you take hearing and understanding God's words? Is your own heart like the polytheist who needed protection just to hear?

The Ash'ari-Maturidi Difference on Takwin and Power's Function
Compares Ash'ari and Maturidi views on takwin and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key theological disagreement between Ash'aris and Maturidis regarding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and how it relates to the function of divine power (qudra).

Core Idea
The debate over takwin reveals deeper differences on how power and will work.

This passage presents a comparative analysis of the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on the attribute of takwin. The author explains that while both schools agree that things are brought from non-existence to existence, they differ on the role of power and whether takwin is an additional attribute. The Ash'aris argue that power has two attachments—one eternal dispositional and one originated actualizing—and that takwin is merely the latter, not a separate eternal attribute. This disagreement reflects a broader difference in understanding God's attributes of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic and English translation to get an overall sense of the argument. Note the key terms and the contrasting views.
The text mentions Maturidi and Ash'ari positions; try to identify the point of contention.
2
Identify the two attachments of power
Find the description of power's ta'alluq suluhi (dispositional) and ta'alluq tanjizi (actualizing). Understand that for Ash'aris, power has these two attachments.
The passage says power has one eternal dispositional attachment to the possibility of things, and another originated actualizing attachment.
3
Compare the Maturidi and Ash'ari positions on takwin
Notice that Maturidis see takwin as a separate attribute, while Ash'aris consider it to be the same as the actualizing attachment of power, thus not an additional attribute.
The passage states: 'On that basis, the Ash'ari sees no meaning in affirming at-takwin as an additional attribute.'
4
Reflect on the deeper implications
Consider how this difference ties to the broader disagreement about attributes of action (sifat al-fi'l) and the function of power.
The author concludes: 'behind the difference in the attribute of takwin is a difference in the attributes of action and a difference in the attribute of power and its function.'

الماتريدي والأشعري إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود ، غاية ما هناك أن هذا التعلق متوقف على انضمام الإرادة وتابع للعلم، بمعنى أن ما علم الله وجوده يوجد منه بقدرته ، والإرادة تخصص زمان الوقوع . وليس التكوين إلا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور محال إرادة الله إيجاده ثمة كانت صفة نسبية حادثة . فالقدرة عند الأشاعرة لما تعلق صلوحي قديم ، ومن وهو تعلقها بصحة وجود الأشياء ، والآخر تعلق تنجيزي حادث ، وليس التكوين هذا التعلق التنجيزي الحادث الذي هو نفس إخراج الأشياء من العدم إلى الوجود . وعلى ذلك لا يرى الأشعرية معنى لاثبات التكوين صفة زائدة لا فائدة الصفة المؤثرة في إيجاد الأشياء [؟] سبوعي فيها جالا أن القدرة هي إذن فوراء الاختلاف في صفة التكوين اختلاف في صفات الفعل ، واختلاف في صفة القدرة ووظيفتها .
Al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari: bringing them out from non-existence to existence. The utmost there is that this attachment depends on the joining of the will and follows knowledge, meaning that what God knows to exist comes from Him by His power, and the will specifies the time of occurrence. At-takwin is nothing but the attachment of power to the object of power, the locus of God's will to bring it into existence, then it would be a relative, originated attribute. For power according to the Ash'aris has one eternal dispositional attachment, which is its attachment to the possibility of things existing, and another actualizing attachment that is originated, and at-takwin is not this originated actualizing attachment which is the very bringing of things from non-existence to existence. On that basis, the Ash'ari sees no meaning in affirming at-takwin as an additional attribute, no benefit, the effective attribute in bringing things into existence [؟] ... then behind the difference in the attribute of takwin is a difference in the attributes of action and a difference in the attribute of power and its function.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a comparative analysis of the Ash'ari and Maturidi views on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The author explains that the creation of things from non-existence depends on the attachment of power (qudra) to the object, but this attachment requires the will (irada) and follows knowledge ('ilm). God's knowledge determines what will exist, His power executes existence, and His will specifies the time. For the Ash'aris, power has two attachments: one eternal dispositional (ta'alluq suluhi qadim) that relates to the possibility of things, and another originated actualizing (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith) that actually brings things into existence. They argue that takwin is not this originated actualizing attachment but rather a relative attribute. Therefore, they see no need to affirm takwin as a separate attribute, since power itself is effective. The author concludes that the disagreement about takwin reflects a deeper disagreement about the attributes of action and the function of power. The text then transitions to the broader agreement among Ahl al-Sunna.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis on takwin is merely terminological and does not affect other doctrines.
Correction: The passage shows that the disagreement on takwin reflects deeper differences in understanding the attributes of action and the function of power, indicating it is not just terminological.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Ash'aris not affirm takwin as a separate attribute?
A) Because they consider it a property of will.
B) Because they consider power to have an originated actualizing attachment that creates, and takwin is that attachment.
C) Because they believe takwin is a relative and originated attribute, and power already suffices.
D) Because they deny that God has power over creation.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement over takwin centers on whether power's actualizing attachment constitutes a separate attribute, pointing to deeper differences in understanding divine action and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's power, do you imagine it as a static reservoir 'able to do anything' (dispositional) or as a dynamic force actively bringing things into your life at every moment (actualizing)? Which view shapes how you pray and expect answers? If you feel a gap, will you adjust your understanding today?
?
The Ash'aris argued that affirming takwin as a separate attribute has no practical benefit. In your own faith, are there theological distinctions you hold onto that do not affect your worship or trust in God? Could you let them go, or are they worth preserving even if they seem abstract?
?
The passage says that God's will 'specifies the time of occurrence' of what is brought into existence. Do you live as if everything has a divinely appointed time, or do you often feel that opportunities slip away permanently? What would change in your life if you truly believed that God's power and will together ensure the perfect timing of everything you need?

The Consensus of Ahl al-Sunna on Attributes and Kalam Nafsi
Imam Maturidi enumerates two points of consensus among Ahl al-Sunna and introduces the distinction in speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational consensus among Ahl al-Sunna regarding attributes additional to the essence and the distinction between God's eternal internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the created letters and sounds that indicate it.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna agree on eternal attributes and distinguish kalam nafsi from created sounds.

Before presenting sectarian differences, Imam Maturidi emphasizes the common ground: all Ahl al-Sunna affirm that God's attributes are eternal meanings distinct from but not separate from His essence. They also unanimously agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and they strictly differentiate between the eternal internal speech and the temporal letters and sounds that convey it. This consensus provides the necessary backdrop for understanding the later debate on whether that internal speech can be heard.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on consensus
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice that the author first establishes that no one leaves the circle of Ahl al-Sunna despite differences in branches, then lists the two points of agreement.
2
Identify the first agreement on attributes
Find the statement that Ahl al-Sunna unanimously affirm attributes additional to the essence as eternal meanings, neither identical nor separate.
3
Identify the second agreement on speech
Find where the author states the agreement on speech and the distinction between kalam nafsi and letters/sounds.
4
Understand the significance
Reflect on why this consensus is important before discussing the disagreement on hearing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخرج واحد من دائرة أهل السنة لأنه اختلف أصحابه في تفاريع المذهب ، لأن الأصل ثابت ومتفق عليه وهو إجماع أهل السنة على إثبات الصفات الزائدة على الذات كمعاني قديمة لا [؟] مع لذات ولا هي غير الذات . ويتفق أهل السنة على أن كلام الله تعالى صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته مفرقين بين كلامه النفسي الذي هو صفة له قديمة وبين الحروف والأصوات الدالة على كلامه النفسي وهي عندهم حادثة . ثم يختلفون بعد ذلك حول بجواز سماع كلامه النفسي . فالأشعري ومعظم أصحابه يقولون بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، وطم على ذلك سند من العقل والنقل. أما العقل فقد استند الأشعري في دعواه على جواز الله على نفس الأساس الذي استند عليه في جواز رؤية الله . فكما أن علة جواز كونه مرئياً ، فكذلك وجود الكلام النفسي هو [؟] گونه مسرعاً. أما النقل فيتمسك الأشعري بقوله تعالى : {وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللَّهِ} وقوله تعالى : {وَكَلَّمَ اللَّهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيماً} وقوله تعالى : {وَلَمَّا جَاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيقَاتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُ رَبُّهُ}.
And not one departs from the circle of Ahl al-Sunna, because its adherents differ only in branches of the school, since the principle is established and agreed upon, which is the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna on affirming attributes additional to the essence as eternal meanings, not [؟] with the essences nor are they other than the essence. And Ahl al-Sunna agree that the speech of God Most High is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between His internal speech (kalam nafsi) which is an eternal attribute of Him, and the letters and sounds indicating His internal speech, which are originated in their view. Then they differ after that about the permissibility of hearing His internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers say it is permissible to hear internal speech, and they have for that a proof from reason and transmission. As for reason, al-Ash'ari based his claim on the permissibility of hearing God on the same basis on which he based the permissibility of seeing God. For just as the cause for the permissibility of His being seen, so too the existence of internal speech is [؟] ... As for transmission, al-Ash'ari adheres to His statement: 'And if one of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah,' and His statement: 'And Allah spoke to Moses with [direct] speech,' and His statement: 'And when Moses came to Our appointed time and his Lord spoke to him.'
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage first affirms the foundational agreement among Ahl al-Sunna: they all affirm attributes additional to the essence, which are eternal meanings that are neither identical to the essence nor separate from it. They also agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between the eternal internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the originated letters and sounds that indicate it. The point of disagreement is whether this internal speech can be heard. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers affirm that it can be heard, and they provide both rational and scriptural proofs. The rational proof is analogical: just as they argue for the permissibility of seeing God (ru'ya) based on the attribute of existence being the cause for visibility, similarly the existence of internal speech makes it audible. The scriptural proof cites Quranic verses: the verse about granting protection so that a polytheist may hear the word of Allah (9:6), the verse that Allah spoke to Moses directly (4:164), and the verse that his Lord spoke to him (7:143). These verses imply that the eternal speech was heard by Moses or polytheists, according to Ash'ari interpretation.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
الصفات الزائدة
الحروف والأصوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ahl al-Sunna differ on the existence of eternal attributes.
Correction: The passage affirms that all Ahl al-Sunna agree on affirming attributes additional to the essence; differences are only in branches.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do Ahl al-Sunna view the letters and sounds that indicate God's internal speech?
A) They are eternal like the internal speech.
B) They are created/originated.
C) They are part of God's essence.
D) They do not exist.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute, but the letters and sounds through which it is expressed are created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you focus more on the beauty of the sound or the meaning of God's eternal speech? Which one truly moves your heart? Commit to pausing after each verse today to reflect on its meaning.
?
You learned that Ahl al-Sunna agree on real attributes additional to God's essence. Is there any attribute of God—like His power, mercy, or justice—that you have not allowed to shape how you live? Name one specific way you will let that attribute change your actions this week.

The passage says differences in branches do not remove one from Ahl al-Sunna. Are you quick to judge others who differ with you on minor issues? How can you prioritize the core agreements mentioned in this lesson to build unity in your community? Write one practical step you will take.

The Ash'ari Proof for Hearing Eternal Speech
Imam Maturidi presents the Ash'ari rational analogy and scriptural proofs for hearing kalam nafsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari rational and scriptural arguments for the possibility of hearing God's eternal internal speech (kalam nafsi).

Core Idea
Ash'ari argues hearing kalam nafsi is possible by analogy with seeing Allah, supported by Quran.

Having established the common ground on kalam nafsi, Imam Maturidi now presents the Ash'ari position that this internal speech can be heard. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers provide two proofs: a rational one based on analogy with the permissibility of seeing Allah, and a scriptural one citing verses that mention hearing God's speech. These proofs aim to show that the eternal attribute of speech is perceivable, even though it is not composed of letters and sounds.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari claim and rational proof
Identify the claim that hearing kalam nafsi is permissible and note the rational analogy to the permissibility of seeing Allah.
2
Analyze the rational analogy
Understand that just as existence is the cause for visibility, existence of kalam nafsi makes it audible. This is an extension of the same principle.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
Read the three Quranic verses cited: 9:6, 4:164, 7:143. Consider how they are used to support the audibility of internal speech.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the rational and scriptural proofs together form the Ash'ari case for hearing eternal speech.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخرج واحد من دائرة أهل السنة لأنه اختلف أصحابه في تفاريع المذهب ، لأن الأصل ثابت ومتفق عليه وهو إجماع أهل السنة على إثبات الصفات الزائدة على الذات كمعاني قديمة لا [؟] مع لذات ولا هي غير الذات . ويتفق أهل السنة على أن كلام الله تعالى صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته مفرقين بين كلامه النفسي الذي هو صفة له قديمة وبين الحروف والأصوات الدالة على كلامه النفسي وهي عندهم حادثة . ثم يختلفون بعد ذلك حول بجواز سماع كلامه النفسي . فالأشعري ومعظم أصحابه يقولون بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، وطم على ذلك سند من العقل والنقل. أما العقل فقد استند الأشعري في دعواه على جواز الله على نفس الأساس الذي استند عليه في جواز رؤية الله . فكما أن علة جواز كونه مرئياً ، فكذلك وجود الكلام النفسي هو [؟] گونه مسرعاً. أما النقل فيتمسك الأشعري بقوله تعالى : {وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللَّهِ} وقوله تعالى : {وَكَلَّمَ اللَّهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيماً} وقوله تعالى : {وَلَمَّا جَاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيقَاتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُ رَبُّهُ}.
And not one departs from the circle of Ahl al-Sunna, because its adherents differ only in branches of the school, since the principle is established and agreed upon, which is the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna on affirming attributes additional to the essence as eternal meanings, not [؟] with the essences nor are they other than the essence. And Ahl al-Sunna agree that the speech of God Most High is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between His internal speech (kalam nafsi) which is an eternal attribute of Him, and the letters and sounds indicating His internal speech, which are originated in their view. Then they differ after that about the permissibility of hearing His internal speech. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers say it is permissible to hear internal speech, and they have for that a proof from reason and transmission. As for reason, al-Ash'ari based his claim on the permissibility of hearing God on the same basis on which he based the permissibility of seeing God. For just as the cause for the permissibility of His being seen, so too the existence of internal speech is [؟] ... As for transmission, al-Ash'ari adheres to His statement: 'And if one of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah,' and His statement: 'And Allah spoke to Moses with [direct] speech,' and His statement: 'And when Moses came to Our appointed time and his Lord spoke to him.'

Commentary
This passage first affirms the foundational agreement among Ahl al-Sunna: they all affirm attributes additional to the essence, which are eternal meanings that are neither identical to the essence nor separate from it. They also agree that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinguishing between the eternal internal speech (kalam nafsi) and the originated letters and sounds that indicate it. The point of disagreement is whether this internal speech can be heard. Al-Ash'ari and most of his followers affirm that it can be heard, and they provide both rational and scriptural proofs. The rational proof is analogical: just as they argue for the permissibility of seeing God (ru'ya) based on the attribute of existence being the cause for visibility, similarly the existence of internal speech makes it audible. The scriptural proof cites Quranic verses: the verse about granting protection so that a polytheist may hear the word of Allah (9:6), the verse that Allah spoke to Moses directly (4:164), and the verse that his Lord spoke to him (7:143). These verses imply that the eternal speech was heard by Moses or polytheists, according to Ash'ari interpretation.

The Maturidi Position on Hearing Eternal Speech
The author explains the Maturidi rejection of hearing kalam nafsi and internal differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi stance on whether Moses heard the eternal speech of Allah, their hermeneutical approach, and the internal debate regarding the possibility of hearing internal speech.

Core Idea
Maturidis denied Moses heard eternal speech but debated its possibility.

In this passage, the author examines the Maturidi response to the Ash'ari claim that Moses heard the eternal speech of Allah. The Maturidis reinterpret the Quranic verse to mean hearing the indicators of speech, not the speech itself. However, they were not unanimous: while al-Maturidi himself remained ambiguous, his followers split over whether internal speech could ever be heard, leading to a deeper discussion about the conditions for hearing versus vision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the author's summary of the Maturidi position and the internal disagreement.
2
Identify the core argument
The Maturidis do not find evidence that Moses heard the eternal speech itself. They reinterpret 'hearing the word of Allah' as hearing what indicates it.
Look for the analogies: 'I heard so-and-so's knowledge' and 'look at the power of God'.
3
Note the internal divergence
Al-Maturidi himself did not explicitly forbid or allow hearing kalam nafsi, but some followers affirmed its possibility, while others required letter and sound.
The author cites al-Shaykh Zadah for the permissive opinion.
4
Understand the cause vs condition distinction
Those who deny hearing kalam nafsi distinguish between a real cause (letter/sound) and customary conditions (like distance for vision). This blocks the analogy with ru'ya.
The Mu'tazila's conditions for vision are customary, not causal.
5
Reflect on the consensus
Note the concluding remark: Ahl al-Sunna (Maturidis and Ash'aris) agree on the permissibility of seeing God (ru'ya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الماتريدي وأصحابه فلم يجدوا في هذه الآيات دليلاً على أن موسى سمع كلام الله الأزلي ، وذهبوا إلى أن موسى عليه السلام سمع ما يدل على كلامه الأزلي ، وفسروا قوله تعالى حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللَّهِ بمعنى حتى يسمع ما يدل على كلام الله. وذلك مثل من يقول : سمعت علم فلان ، أي ما يدل على علمه ، كما يقال أيضاً : انظروا إلى قدرة الله أي إلى ما يدل على قدرته . لكن ينبغي أن نلتفت هنا إلى أن الماتريدي وأصحابه وإن كانوا قد أنجالوا سماع موسى لكلام الله النفسي إلا أنهم مختلفون فيما بينهم حول جواز سماع هذا الكلام اشتراطهم للحرف والصوت حتى يكون الكلام مسموعاً. أما الماتريدي نفسه فلم أجد عنده ما يدل على أنه يحيل سماع الكلام النفسي مطلقاً ولم يصرح يشترط لصحة السماع الحرف والصوت. ويحدثنا الشيخ زاده بأن بعض اتباع الماتريدي قد اعترفوا صراحة بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، وأنه غير مستحيل ؛ لأن الله قادر على أن يخلق للقوة السامعة إدراك الكلام النفسي . أما الماتريدية الذين أحالوا سماع الكلام النفسي لاشتراط الصوت والحرف فقد فرقوا بين العلة والشرط العادي ، وبذلك يرفضون قياس السماع على الرؤية ؛ لأن ما يذكره المعتزلة من شروط للرؤية ليست إلا شروطاً عادية للرؤية وليست عللاً حقيقية للرؤية ؟ وذلك بخلاف الصوت والحرف لأنهما علتان حقيقيتان للسماع . والإجماع منعقد بين أهل السنة من الماتريدية والأشعرية على جواز رؤية الله
As for al-Maturidi and his followers, they did not find in these verses evidence that Moses heard the eternal speech of God, and they held that Moses, peace be upon him, heard what indicates His eternal speech, and they interpreted His statement 'until he hears the word of Allah' to mean 'until he hears what indicates the word of Allah.' That is like one who says: 'I heard the knowledge of so-and-so,' meaning what indicates his knowledge, just as it is also said: 'Look at the power of God,' meaning at what indicates His power. But it should be noted here that al-Maturidi and his followers, although they denied that Moses heard the internal speech of God, nevertheless differ among themselves regarding the permissibility of hearing this speech, because they stipulate letter and sound for speech to be heard. As for al-Maturidi himself, I did not find from him anything indicating that he absolutely considers hearing internal speech impossible, nor did he explicitly stipulate letter and sound for the validity of hearing. And al-Shaykh Zadah informs us that some followers of al-Maturidi explicitly acknowledged the permissibility of hearing internal speech, and that it is not impossible, because God is able to create for the hearing faculty the perception of internal speech. As for the Maturidis who considered hearing internal speech impossible due to stipulating sound and letter, they distinguished between the [real] cause and the customary condition, and thereby they reject the analogy of hearing with vision, because what the Mu'tazila mention as conditions for vision are only customary conditions for vision and not real causes for vision, unlike sound and letter, for they are real causes for hearing. And there is consensus among Ahl al-Sunna, both Maturidis and Ash'aris, on the permissibility of seeing God.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on hearing the eternal speech (kalam nafsi). Al-Maturidi and his followers argue that the Quranic verses cited by the Ash'aris do not prove that Moses actually heard the eternal speech itself. Instead, they interpret 'hearing the word of Allah' as hearing what indicates that speech, such as the letters and sounds that express the eternal meaning. They provide analogies: one can say 'I heard so-and-so's knowledge' meaning I heard words that indicate his knowledge, or 'look at the power of God' meaning look at evidence of His power. The author then notes that although Maturidis deny that Moses heard the eternal speech, they differ among themselves on whether such hearing is possible in principle. Al-Maturidi himself does not explicitly rule out the possibility nor does he require letter and sound for hearing to occur. Some later Maturidis, according to al-Shaykh Zadah, explicitly affirm the possibility, since God could create in the hearing faculty the perception of internal speech without sound. Those Maturidis who deny the possibility because they require sound and letter for any hearing distinguish between a real cause ('illa) and a customary condition (shart 'adi). They argue that the conditions for vision (like distance, intervening medium) are merely customary, not real causes, so hearing cannot be analogized to vision. In contrast, sound and letter are real causes for hearing, so internal speech cannot be heard without them. Finally, the author notes the consensus among Ahl al-Sunna (both Maturidis and Ash'aris) on the possibility of seeing God (ru'ya).

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
السماع
العلة
الشرط العادي
الرؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi position is unanimously that hearing kalam nafsi is impossible.
Correction: Al-Maturidi himself did not explicitly forbid it, and some later Maturidis affirmed the possibility through divine power.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the Maturidi position from the Ash'ari on hearing kalam nafsi?
A) Maturidis unanimously deny the possibility of hearing it, unlike Ash'aris.
B) Maturidis do not find scriptural evidence that Moses heard the eternal speech, and they interpret hearing as hearing what indicates it.
C) Maturidis insist that hearing requires letters and sounds, so it is impossible.
D) Maturidis reject the analogy with vision because they consider vision to be impossible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi and his followers denied that Moses heard eternal speech itself but differed on its possibility, using a cause-condition distinction to counter analogies with vision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you treat it as merely words on a page, or do you seek to encounter the eternal speech of your Lord behind them? What would change in your recitation if you truly believed you were hearing from God Himself?
?
The Maturidis held that Moses heard only what points to God's eternal speech. Are you satisfied with 'hearing about' God from scholars and texts, or are you desperate to hear His voice directly in your heart through His book? What steps will you take this week to listen to the Quran as if it were being revealed to you now?
?
If God can create in you the perception of His internal speech apart from sounds and letters, why do you still rely on your own intellectual grasp of theology rather than begging Him to make you truly hear His words? Will you today ask Him to open your ears to the meaning of His speech beyond your limited understanding?

Maturidi on Hearing God's Speech
Maturidi explains that Musa only heard what indicates God's speech, not the eternal word itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's interpretation of how Prophet Musa heard God's speech, distinguishing between the eternal divine word and what indicates it.

Core Idea
Hearing God's speech does not require hearing the eternal word itself.

In this lesson, we explore how Imam al-Maturidi reconciled verses about Musa hearing God's speech with his theological principles. He argued that these verses refer to hearing what indicates God's eternal word, not the word itself, drawing on linguistic analogies. We will also see the range of opinions among his followers on the possibility of hearing internal speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation once through. Let the author's presentation of different positions sink in before analysis.
Note the three Quranic verses cited at the start.
2
Identify Maturidi's interpretative method
Maturidi does not take the verses literally. He interprets 'hearing the word of God' as 'hearing what indicates it'. Spot the analogies he uses (e.g., hearing someone's knowledge).
This is key to his approach.
3
Understand the internal disagreement
Notice that while Maturidis agree that Musa did not hear the eternal word, they differ on whether hearing internal speech is possible in principle. Some require letter/sound; Maturidi himself does not explicitly forbid it.
Shaykhzada reports that some followers affirm its possibility.
4
Reflect on the takeaway
Ask yourself: Why does Maturidi make this distinction? How does it protect God's transcendence while still honoring the Quranic verses?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَع كَلام الله ، وقوله تعالى : للهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيماً ٢٠ وقوله تعالى . وَلَمَّا جَاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيقَاتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُ رَبَّهُ . أما الماتريدي وأصحابه فلم يجدوا في هذه الآيات دليلاً على أن موسى سمع كلام الله الأزلي ، وذهبوا إلى أن [؟] الأزلي ، وفسروا قوله تعالى حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ الله بمعنى حتى يسمع ما يدل على كلام الله . وذلك مثل من يقول : سمعت علم فلان ، أي ما يدل على علمه ، كما يقال أيضاً : انظروا إلى قدرة الله أي إلى ما يدل على قدرته . لكن ينبغي أن نلتفت هنا إلى أن الماتريدي وأصحابه وإن كانوا قد أنجالوا[؟] سماع موسى لكلام الله النفسي إلا أنهم مختلفون فيما بينهم حول جواز سماع هذا الكلام اشتراطهم للحرف والصوت حتى يكون الكلام مسموعاً. أما الماتريدي نفسه فلم أجد عنده ما يدل على أنه يحيل سماع الكلام النفسي مطلقاً ولم يصرح يشترط لصحة السماع الحرف والصوت. ويحدثنا الشيخ زاده بأن بعض اتباع الماتريدي قد اعترفوا صراحة بجواز سماع الكلام النفسي ، وأنه غير مستحيل ؛ لأن الله قادر على أن يخلق للقوة السامعة إدراك الكلام النفسي.
The polytheists seek your protection, so grant them protection until they hear the word of God (kalam Allah). And His saying: 'And God spoke to Moses with [direct] speech.' And His saying: 'And when Moses came to Our appointed time and his Lord spoke to him.' But al-Maturidi and his companions did not find in these verses any evidence that Moses heard the eternal word of God (kalam Allah al-azali), and they held that... the eternal, and they interpreted His saying 'until they hear the word of God' to mean 'until he hears what indicates the word of God.' That is like someone saying: 'I heard the knowledge of so-and-so,' meaning what indicates his knowledge, just as it is also said: 'Look at the power of God,' meaning at what indicates His power. But we should note here that al-Maturidi and his companions, although they [؟] Moses' hearing of the internal speech (kalam allah al-nafsi), yet they differ among themselves regarding the permissibility of hearing this speech, because they require letter and sound (al-harf wa al-sawt) for speech to be audible. As for al-Maturidi himself, I did not find from him anything indicating that he absolutely forbids hearing the internal speech, nor did he explicitly stipulate letter and sound for the validity of hearing. And Shaykhzada informs us that some followers of al-Maturidi explicitly acknowledged the permissibility of hearing the internal speech, and that it is not impossible, because God is able to create for the auditory faculty the perception of the internal speech.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage clarifies Maturidi's position on whether Moses heard the eternal word of God. The author first cites three Quranic verses that are often used to argue that Moses heard God's speech: the verse about granting asylum to polytheists 'until they hear the word of God', the verse stating 'God spoke to Moses directly', and the verse about Moses coming to the appointed time and his Lord speaking to him. Maturidi and his followers, however, did not see these verses as proof that Moses heard the eternal speech itself. They interpreted 'until they hear the word of God' to mean 'until he hears what indicates the word of God', drawing an analogy with phrases like 'I heard the knowledge of so-and-so' (meaning I heard what indicates his knowledge) or 'Look at the power of God' (meaning look at what indicates His power). Thus, they distinguished between hearing the actual eternal speech and hearing something that points to it. The author then notes an internal disagreement among Maturidis: while they all denied that Moses heard the internal speech (kalam nafsi), they differed on whether such hearing is possible in principle. Some required letter and sound (hurf wa sawt) for audibility, thus deeming hearing internal speech impossible. However, al-Maturidi himself did not explicitly forbid hearing internal speech nor require letter and sound. Moreover, Shaykhzada reports that some Maturidi followers affirmed the possibility of hearing internal speech, arguing that God can create for the hearing faculty the perception of internal speech directly.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
الحرف والصوت
سماع كلام الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidi absolutely denies the possibility of hearing God's speech altogether.
Correction: The passage shows Maturidi avoids explicit denial and some of his followers affirm its possibility.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maturidi, how did he interpret the phrase 'until they hear the word of God'?
A) He took it literally as hearing the eternal speech.
B) He interpreted it as hearing what indicates God's speech.
C) He considered it abrogated.
D) He rejected the verse as unreliable.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi distinguishes between the eternal divine word and its indicational hearing, leaving room for the possibility of hearing internal speech without requiring sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Maturidi teaches that you may hear what indicates God's speech rather than the eternal word itself. When you listen to the Quran, do you settle for the sounds and meanings, or do you strive to perceive the divine address behind them? What would change in your worship if you truly heard God speaking through every verse?
?
The passage reports that some scholars affirmed the possibility of hearing internal speech without sound. Have you ever experienced a moment when you felt God was speaking to your heart beyond words? If so, did you trust that experience or dismiss it? If not, are you open to the possibility that God may communicate with you in ways deeper than audible speech?
?
If God can create in you the perception of His internal speech, what does that imply about the closeness He desires with you? Are you actively seeking that kind of direct encounter, or are you satisfied with mediated forms of knowledge? What would you need to change in your spiritual life to be ready for such a hearing?
