The Sunni Consensus on Seeing God
Consensus statement on ru'ya and internal Sunni difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unanimous Sunni position that seeing God is possible without modality, and the internal difference on whether this is known by reason or revelation alone.

Core Idea
Sunni consensus affirms vision of God without modality, but they differ on the proof source.

Before examining the verses, Imam Maturidi establishes the baseline: all Sunnis agree that seeing God in the afterlife is possible, but they disagree whether reason or only transmitted texts prove it. This sets the stage for his clever refutation of the Mu'tazila using their own arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus statement
Read the Arabic sentence stating the consensus among Maturidis and Ash'aris on the permissibility of seeing God without modality.
Notice the phrase 'bila kayfiyya' – without modality.
2
Identify the internal difference
Look at the next part: Sunnis differ on whether this is proven by reason or only by transmitted evidence.
This difference does not break consensus on the doctrine itself.
3
Appreciate the strategic move
The author calls it 'interesting' that Sunnis use the very verses the Mu'tazila cite to deny vision as evidence for affirming it.
This is a key polemical approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإجماع منعقد بين أهل السنة من الماتريدية والأشعرية على جواز رؤية الله بلا كيفية ، ولكنهم يختلفون بعد ذلك فيما بينهم على أن ذلك هل يعلم بدليل من العقل أو أن ذلك مرده إلى النقل وحده . أما النقل فلا خلاف بينهم . ومن الطريف أن يتخذ أهل السنة من الآيات التي احتجت بها المعتزلة نفي الرؤية دليلا على إثبات الرؤية . احتجت المعتزلة على نفي الرؤية بقوله تعالى : لا تُدْرِكْهُ الأَبْصَارُ ، ٢ ، وقوله تعالى لموسى ولَنْ تَرَانِي وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرِ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْيا أو وَرَاءَ حِجَاب . ورأى أهل السنة في قوله تعالى لا تُدرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ، دليلاً على اثبات الرؤية ، إذ الآية من لا تنفي الرؤية وإنما تنفي الإدراك ؛ لأن فيه معنى الإحاطة ، والله منزه عن الإحاطة من جميع الجوانب. أما قوله تعالى لموسى لن تراني ، حين سأله رَبِّ أَرنِي أَنفُلَرْ إِلَيْكَ ١٤ فمعناه أنه لن يراه في الدنيا . ثم لو كان موسى يعلم أن رؤية الله مستحيلة كاستحالة أن يتخذ ولدا أو شريكاً لما سألها الله ؛ إذ كيف يليق بمقام النبرة أن يسأل الله ما لا يليق بجلاله وعظمته ، ولكان سؤال موسى جهلاً يبلغ درجة الكفر ، والكان الله نهاه وعاتبه كما نهى نوحاً وعاتب آدم في غير هذا . ولكنه تعالى لم ينهنه ولا أياسه وإنما شرط الرؤية باستقرار الجبل فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرٌّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي واستقرار الجبل أمر ممكن في ذاته ، وما شرط بالممكن فهو ممكن : " ولقد اندك الجبل فلما تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَل جَعَلَهُ دَكَ وَخَرَّ مُوسَى صَعِتا " ، ليعلم الله أنه لن يراه في الدنيا . ثم كيف يدعي المعتزلة العلم باستحالة الرؤية ويجهلها موسى .
And there is consensus among Ahl al-Sunna, both Maturidis and Ash'aris, on the permissibility of seeing God without modality (bila kayfiyya). However, they differ among themselves as to whether this is known by a rational proof or is only based on transmitted evidence (naql). As for the transmitted evidence, there is no disagreement among them. And it is interesting that Ahl al-Sunna take the verses that the Mu'tazilites used to deny vision as evidence to affirm vision. The Mu'tazilites argued for the denial of vision by His saying: 'Eyes comprehend Him not' (la tudrikuhu al-absar), and His words to Moses: 'You will not see Me', and 'It is not for a human that God should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil.' And Ahl al-Sunna saw in His saying 'Eyes comprehend Him not' a proof for affirming vision, because the verse does not deny vision but rather denies comprehension (idrak), for it has the meaning of encompassment, and God is transcendent beyond encompassment from all sides. As for His words to Moses: 'You will not see Me' when he asked: 'My Lord, show me that I may look at You,' its meaning is that he will not see Him in this world. Then, if Moses knew that seeing God is as impossible as taking a son or partner, he would not have asked for it; for how is it befitting the station of prophecy to ask God for what does not befit His majesty and greatness? And Moses' question would be ignorance reaching the level of disbelief. And God would have forbidden him and reproached him just as He forbade Noah and reproached Adam in other cases. But He did not forbid him nor discourage him, but rather conditioned the vision on the stability of the mountain: 'If it remains in its place, then you will see Me.' And the stability of the mountain is possible in itself, and what is conditioned by the possible is itself possible. And the mountain crumbled when his Lord revealed Himself to it, and made it flat, and Moses fell down stunned, so that God might know that he will not see Him in this world. Then how can the Mu'tazilites claim knowledge of the impossibility of vision when Moses was ignorant of it?
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage covers the Sunni position on the vision (ru'ya) of God and their response to the Mu'tazilite objection. First, it states that there is a consensus among Ahl al-Sunna (both Maturidis and Ash'aris) that seeing God is permissible 'without modality' (bila kayfiyya). They differ, however, on whether this is established by rational proof or solely by transmitted evidence (naql). Nonetheless, they agree on the transmitted evidence. Then the author notes the interesting strategy of Ahl al-Sunna: they use the very verses that the Mu'tazilites cite to deny vision as proofs for affirming it. The Mu'tazilites relied on three proofs: 'Eyes comprehend Him not' (la tudrikuhu al-absar), the words to Moses 'You will not see Me' (lan tarani), and the statement that God only speaks to humans by revelation or from behind a veil. Ahl al-Sunna interpret the first verse as denying 'comprehension' (idrak), which implies encompassment, not denying vision itself. They then explain the second verse by pointing out that it refers to this world: Moses will not see God in the world. They use a powerful argument: if Moses had known that seeing God is impossible in itself—as impossible as God having a partner—then he would never have asked for it, because it would be an ignorant request unbefitting a prophet. God would have rebuked him as He rebuked other prophets for lesser things. Instead, God did not forbid him but conditioned the vision on the mountain's stability. Since the mountain's stability is possible, the vision conditioned on it is also possible. The mountain crumbled when God manifested Himself, showing that Moses would not see Him in this world. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: how can the Mu'tazilites claim to know the impossibility of vision when even Moses was ignorant of it?

Key Terms
الرؤية
بلا كيفية
الماتريدية
الأشعرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all Muslims agree on the rational proof for seeing God.
Correction: Sunnis agree on the doctrine, but differ on whether reason alone proves it or only revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the difference among Sunnis regarding the proof for seeing God?
A) Some say it is impossible, others possible.
B) Some say it is known by reason, others only by transmitted texts.
C) Some say it is known by consensus, others by analogy.
D) There is no difference; all use reason.

Key Takeaway
Sunnis unanimously affirm the possibility of seeing God without modality, but they debate whether reason or revelation alone establishes this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on reason or on transmitted texts in your faith? The Sunnis disagree on which proves ru'ya, but they unite on the reality. Where in your life do you let minor disagreements break your unity with fellow Muslims? Will you change that starting today?
?
The Mu'tazila used verses to deny seeing God, but Sunnis reinterpreted them to affirm it. Have you ever dismissed a verse or hadith because it seemed to contradict your understanding? What would it take for you to reconsider your interpretation with humility?
?
If you knew you would see Allah on the Day of Judgment, how would it change your actions right now? Are you willing to live as if that vision is certain, even if you cannot grasp the 'how'?

Reinterpreting 'Eyes Comprehend Him Not'
Sunni interpretation of 'Eyes comprehend Him not'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna interpret the verse 'Eyes comprehend Him not' not as a denial of vision but as a denial of total encompassment.

Core Idea
Comprehension (idrak) is not vision; the verse denies encompassment, not sight.

The Mu'tazila cite the Quranic verse 'Eyes comprehend Him not' as proof that God cannot be seen. But Sunnis turn it around: the Arabic word idrak means full encompassment, which is impossible for God, but simple vision (ru'ya) remains possible. This lesson examines that linguistic and theological nuance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's proof
Read the first part: the Mu'tazila use the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' to deny vision.
2
Analyze the Sunni response
Notice how Sunnis argue that the word 'idrak' means 'comprehension' or 'encompassment', not just 'seeing'.
They say the verse only denies full encompassment, not the act of seeing.
3
Understand the implications
Reflect on why this distinction matters: it allows affirming vision while upholding God's transcendence.
God is beyond full encompassment, but can be seen without limitation.

The Moses Verse and the Conditional Proof
Sunni interpretation of Moses verse and conditional proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni argument for the possibility of seeing God based on the story of Moses and God's condition of the mountain's stability.

Core Idea
God conditioned vision on a possible event, proving it is possible.

The Mu'tazila also cite God's words to Moses, 'You will not see Me,' as evidence of impossibility. But Sunnis explain that this was a temporary denial in this world, and they use the condition of the mountain to prove that vision is possible in principle. This lesson unpacks that powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's second proof
Read the part where Mu'tazila use 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me) against Moses.
2
Understand the Sunni explanation
Sunnis say this refers to this world only, not the afterlife. Then they argue: if Moses knew it was impossible, he wouldn't have asked.
Moses' request shows he considered it possible.
3
Analyze the conditional argument
God conditioned vision on the mountain's stability – if it stays, you will see Me. Since the mountain's stability is possible, the conditioned vision is also possible.
The mountain crumbled, but that only proves it didn't happen in this world.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'lan tarani' proves vision is impossible in any sense.
Correction: Sunnis show it only denies vision in this world, and the conditional argument proves its possibility.

Checkpoint
What does the Sunni author say about God's response to Moses' request?
A) God immediately refused and rebuked Moses.
B) God conditioned vision on the mountain's stability.
C) God told Moses to ask again later.
D) God showed Moses a vision of Himself.

Key Takeaway
By conditioning vision on a possible event, God showed that seeing Him is possible, even if it did not occur in this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Moses, a prophet who spoke to Allah, earnestly begged to see Him. Do you truly yearn to see Allah with the eyes of your heart in this life, or have you grown content with spiritual blindness? What will you do today to increase that longing?
?
Allah did not rebuke Moses but instead gave a sign. When your duas seem unanswered, do you trust Allah's wisdom and wait for His sign, or do you let impatience and doubt creep in? Will you commit to waiting upon His condition?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed certainty that Allah cannot be seen. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that you have never honestly questioned or verified from the Quran and Sunnah? Will you humble yourself like Moses and seek deeper knowledge even if it shakes your assumptions?
